<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Levi-Civita symbol</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Levi-Civita_connection" title="Levi-Civita connection">Levi-Civita connection</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See <a href="/wiki/Ricci_calculus" title="Ricci calculus">Ricci calculus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Einstein_notation" title="Einstein notation">Einstein notation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Raising_and_lowering_indices" title="Raising and lowering indices">Raising and lowering indices</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Index_notation" title="Index notation">index notation</a> used in the article.</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Linear_algebra" title="Linear algebra">linear algebra</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tensor_analysis" title="Tensor analysis">tensor analysis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Differential_geometry" title="Differential geometry">differential geometry</a>, the <b>Levi-Civita symbol</b> represents a collection of numbers; defined from the <a href="/wiki/Parity_of_a_permutation" title="Parity of a permutation">sign of a permutation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a> <span class="texhtml">1, 2, …, <i>n</i></span>, for some positive integer <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>. It is named after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a> <a href="/wiki/Mathematician" title="Mathematician">mathematician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicist</a> <a href="/wiki/Tullio_Levi-Civita" title="Tullio Levi-Civita">Tullio Levi-Civita</a>. Other names include the <b><a href="/wiki/Permutation" title="Permutation">permutation</a> symbol</b>, <b>antisymmetric symbol</b>, or <b>alternating symbol</b>, which refer to its <a href="/wiki/Antisymmetric_tensor" title="Antisymmetric tensor">antisymmetric</a> property and definition in terms of permutations.</p>
<p>The standard letters to denote the Levi-Civita symbol are the <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">Greek</a> lower case <a href="/wiki/Epsilon" title="Epsilon">epsilon</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ε</span> or <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ϵ</span>, or less commonly the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin</a> lower case <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">e</span>. <a href="/wiki/Index_notation" title="Index notation">Index notation</a> allows one to display permutations in a way compatible with tensor analysis:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{i_{1}i_{2}\dots i_{n}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{i_{1}i_{2}\dots i_{n}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/75be000de23194d18b8e0426ea0e43f592964fd8" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:7.63ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <i>each</i> index <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i><sub>1</sub>, <i>i</i><sub>2</sub>, …, <i>i</i><sub><i>n</i></sub></span> takes values <span class="texhtml">1, 2, …, <i>n</i></span>. There are <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n<sup>n</sup></span> indexed values of <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i><sub><i>i</i><sub>1</sub><i>i</i><sub>2</sub>…<i>i<sub>n</sub></i></sub></span>, which can be arranged into an <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>-dimensional array. The key definitive property of the symbol is <i>total <a href="/wiki/Antisymmetric_tensor" title="Antisymmetric tensor">antisymmetry</a></i> in all the indices. When any two indices are interchanged, equal or not, the symbol is negated:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>q</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>q</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{\dots i_{p}\dots i_{q}\dots }=-\varepsilon _{\dots i_{q}\dots i_{p}\dots }.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{\dots i_{p}\dots i_{q}\dots }=-\varepsilon _{\dots i_{q}\dots i_{p}\dots }.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/35d766798eabbe2dee596bc417931838a4ac3842" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:25.386ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>If any two indices are equal, the symbol is zero. When all indices are unequal, we have:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>12</mn>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{i_{1}i_{2}\dots i_{n}}=(-1)^{p}\varepsilon _{12\dots n},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{i_{1}i_{2}\dots i_{n}}=(-1)^{p}\varepsilon _{12\dots n},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5e56afcdafbf76d5e13da44a4c8689025b12ffde" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:23.196ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">p</span> (called the parity of the permutation) is the number of interchanges of indices necessary to unscramble <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i><sub>1</sub>, <i>i</i><sub>2</sub>, …, <i>i</i><sub><i>n</i></sub></span> into the order <span class="texhtml">1, 2, …, <i>n</i></span>, and the factor <span class="texhtml">(−1)<sup><i>p</i></sup></span> is called the <a href="/wiki/Parity_of_a_permutation" title="Parity of a permutation">sign or signature</a> of the permutation. The value <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i><sub>12…<i>n</i></sub></span> must be defined, else the particular values of the symbol for all permutations are indeterminate. Most authors choose <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i><sub>12…<i>n</i></sub> = +1</span>, which means the Levi-Civita symbol equals the sign of a permutation when the indices are all unequal. This choice is used throughout this article.</p>
<p>The term "<span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>-dimensional Levi-Civita symbol" refers to the fact that the number of indices on the symbol <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> matches the <a href="/wiki/Dimension" title="Dimension">dimensionality</a> of the relevant <a href="/wiki/Vector_space" title="Vector space">vector space</a> in question, which may be <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_space" title="Euclidean space">Euclidean</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Euclidean_space" title="Non-Euclidean space">non-Euclidean</a>, pure space or <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">spacetime</a>. The values of the Levi-Civita symbol are independent of any <a href="/wiki/Metric_tensor" title="Metric tensor">metric tensor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coordinate_system" title="Coordinate system">coordinate system</a>. Also, the specific term "symbol" emphasizes that it is not a <a href="/wiki/Tensor" title="Tensor">tensor</a> because of how it transforms between coordinate systems, however it can be interpreted as a <a href="/wiki/Tensor_density" title="Tensor density">tensor density</a>.</p>
<p>The Levi-Civita symbol allows the <a href="/wiki/Determinant" title="Determinant">determinant</a> of a square matrix, and the <a href="/wiki/Cross_product" title="Cross product">cross product</a> of two vectors in three-dimensional Euclidean space, to be expressed in <a href="/wiki/Index_notation" title="Index notation">index notation</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The common dimensionalities of the Levi-Civita symbol are in three and four dimensions, and to some extent two dimensions, so it is useful to see these definitions before the general one in any number of dimensions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Two_dimensions">Two dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Two dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Two_dimensions" title="Two dimensions">two-dimensional</a> Levi-Civita symbol is defined by:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</dl>
<p>Use of the two-dimensional symbol is relatively uncommon, although in certain specialized topics like <a href="/wiki/Supersymmetry" title="Supersymmetry">supersymmetry</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Twistor_theory" title="Twistor theory">twistor theory</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> it appears in the context of 2-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spinors" title="Spinors">spinors</a>. The three- and higher-dimensional Levi-Civita symbols are used more commonly.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_dimensions">Three dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Three dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="208" data-file-width="388" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg/220px-Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg/330px-Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg/440px-Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Permutation_indices_3d_numerical.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
For the indices <span class="texhtml">(<i>i</i>, <i>j</i>, <i>k</i>)</span> in <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ε<sub>ijk</sub></span>, the values <span class="nowrap">1, 2, 3</span> occurring in the <span style="background-color:orange; color:; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">    </span> cyclic order <span class="nowrap">(1, 2, 3)</span> correspond to <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i> = +1</span>, while occurring in the <span style="background-color:red; color:; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">    </span> reverse cyclic order correspond to <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i> = −1</span>, otherwise <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i> = 0</span>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Three_dimensions" title="Three dimensions">three dimensions</a>, the Levi-Civita symbol is defined as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tyldesley_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tyldesley-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow>
<mo>{</mo>
<mtable columnalign="left left" columnspacing="1em" displaystyle="false" rowspacing=".2em">
<mtr>
<mtd>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{ijk}={\begin{cases}+1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k){\text{ is }}(1,2,3),(2,3,1),{\text{ or }}(3,1,2),\\-1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k){\text{ is }}(3,2,1),(1,3,2),{\text{ or }}(2,1,3),\\\;\;\,0&amp;{\text{if }}i=j,{\text{ or }}j=k,{\text{ or }}k=i\end{cases}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{ijk}={\begin{cases}+1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k){\text{ is }}(1,2,3),(2,3,1),{\text{ or }}(3,1,2),\\-1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k){\text{ is }}(3,2,1),(1,3,2),{\text{ or }}(2,1,3),\\\;\;\,0&amp;{\text{if }}i=j,{\text{ or }}j=k,{\text{ or }}k=i\end{cases}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/903ee1efe5f3e041da93aac5f55c82679c3329ad" style="vertical-align: -3.838ex; width:54.644ex; height:8.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>That is, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ε<sub>ijk</sub></span> is 1 if <span class="texhtml">(<i>i</i>, <i>j</i>, <i>k</i>)</span> is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Even_and_odd_permutations" title="Even and odd permutations">even permutation</a> of <span class="nowrap">(1, 2, 3)</span>, −1 if it is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odd_permutation" title="Odd permutation">odd permutation</a>, and 0 if any index is repeated. In three dimensions only, the <a href="/wiki/Cyclic_permutation" title="Cyclic permutation">cyclic permutations</a> of <span class="nowrap">(1, 2, 3)</span> are all even permutations, similarly the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anticyclic_permutation" title="Anticyclic permutation">anticyclic permutations</a> are all odd permutations. This means in 3d it is sufficient to take cyclic or anticyclic permutations of (1,2,3) and easily obtain all the even or odd permutations.</p>
<p>Analogous to 2-dimensional matrices, the values of the 3-dimensional Levi-Civita symbol can be arranged into a <span class="nowrap">3 × 3 × 3</span> array:</p>
<dl>
<dd><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Epsilontensor.svg"><img alt="Epsilontensor.svg" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="500" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Epsilontensor.svg/200px-Epsilontensor.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Epsilontensor.svg/300px-Epsilontensor.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Epsilontensor.svg/400px-Epsilontensor.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span> is the depth(blue,<span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span>=1;red,<span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span>=2;green,<span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span>=3), <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">j</span> the row and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">k</span> the column.</p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}}&amp;=-1\\\varepsilon _{\color {Violet}{3}\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Violet}{3}}&amp;=-(-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}})=1\\\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}\color {BrickRed}{1}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}&amp;=-(-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}})=1\\\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}&amp;=0\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}}&amp;=-1\\\varepsilon _{\color {Violet}{3}\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Violet}{3}}&amp;=-(-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}})=1\\\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}\color {BrickRed}{1}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}&amp;=-(-\varepsilon _{\color {BrickRed}{1}\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}})=1\\\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}=-\varepsilon _{\color {Orange}{2}\color {Violet}{3}\color {Orange}{2}}&amp;=0\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6b24d2da21b82ebed1afec775b13bb8f998d2fa0" style="vertical-align: -5.505ex; width:29.98ex; height:12.176ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four_dimensions">Four dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Four dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Four-dimensional_space" title="Four-dimensional space">four dimensions</a>, the Levi-Civita symbol is defined as:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>
<mi>k</mi>
<mi>l</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow>
<mo>{</mo>
<mtable columnalign="left left" columnspacing="1em" displaystyle="false" rowspacing=".2em">
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>if </mtext>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>j</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>k</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>l</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext> is an even permutation of </mtext>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>2</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>3</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>4</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mtd>
</mtr>
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>if </mtext>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>j</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>k</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>l</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext> is an odd permutation of </mtext>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>2</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>3</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>4</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mtd>
</mtr>
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mspace width="thickmathspace"></mspace>
<mspace width="thickmathspace"></mspace>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
<mn>0</mn>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>otherwise</mtext>
</mrow>
</mtd>
</mtr>
</mtable>
<mo fence="true" stretchy="true"></mo>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{ijkl}={\begin{cases}+1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k,l){\text{ is an even permutation of }}(1,2,3,4)\\-1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k,l){\text{ is an odd permutation of }}(1,2,3,4)\\\;\;\,0&amp;{\text{otherwise}}\end{cases}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{ijkl}={\begin{cases}+1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k,l){\text{ is an even permutation of }}(1,2,3,4)\\-1&amp;{\text{if }}(i,j,k,l){\text{ is an odd permutation of }}(1,2,3,4)\\\;\;\,0&amp;{\text{otherwise}}\end{cases}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/88529e14cefd260f97a6165da0a58ef2c778c0fa" style="vertical-align: -3.838ex; width:62.203ex; height:8.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>These values can be arranged into a <span class="nowrap">4 × 4 × 4 × 4</span> array, although in 4 dimensions and higher this is difficult to draw.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generalization_to_n_dimensions">Generalization to <i><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span></i> dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Generalization to n dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Levi-Civita symbol can be generalized to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N-dimensional_space" title="N-dimensional space"><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> dimensions</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kay_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kay-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{a_{1}a_{2}a_{3}\ldots a_{n}}={\begin{cases}+1&amp;{\text{if }}(a_{1},a_{2},a_{3},\ldots ,a_{n}){\text{ is an even permutation of }}(1,2,3,\dots ,n)\\-1&amp;{\text{if }}(a_{1},a_{2},a_{3},\ldots ,a_{n}){\text{ is an odd permutation of }}(1,2,3,\dots ,n)\\\;\;\,0&amp;{\text{otherwise}}\end{cases}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{a_{1}a_{2}a_{3}\ldots a_{n}}={\begin{cases}+1&amp;{\text{if }}(a_{1},a_{2},a_{3},\ldots ,a_{n}){\text{ is an even permutation of }}(1,2,3,\dots ,n)\\-1&amp;{\text{if }}(a_{1},a_{2},a_{3},\ldots ,a_{n}){\text{ is an odd permutation of }}(1,2,3,\dots ,n)\\\;\;\,0&amp;{\text{otherwise}}\end{cases}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/23c0782db4dd1de2fb3c92a86bc0275bc5dae0cf" style="vertical-align: -3.838ex; width:82.734ex; height:8.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>Thus, it is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Even_and_odd_permutations" title="Even and odd permutations">sign of the permutation</a> in the case of a permutation, and zero otherwise.</p>
<p>Using the <a href="/wiki/Multiplication#Capital_Pi_notation" title="Multiplication">capital pi notation</a> <span class="texhtml">∏</span> for ordinary multiplication of numbers, an explicit expression for the symbol is:</p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\varepsilon _{a_{1}a_{2}a_{3}\ldots a_{n}}&amp;=\prod _{1\leq i&lt;j\leq n}\operatorname {sgn}(a_{j}-a_{i})\\&amp;=\operatorname {sgn}(a_{2}-a_{1})\operatorname {sgn}(a_{3}-a_{1})\dots \operatorname {sgn}(a_{n}-a_{1})\operatorname {sgn}(a_{3}-a_{2})\operatorname {sgn}(a_{4}-a_{2})\dots \operatorname {sgn}(a_{n}-a_{2})\dots \operatorname {sgn}(a_{n}-a_{n-1})\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\varepsilon _{a_{1}a_{2}a_{3}\ldots a_{n}}&amp;=\prod _{1\leq i&lt;j\leq n}\operatorname {sgn}(a_{j}-a_{i})\\&amp;=\operatorname {sgn}(a_{2}-a_{1})\operatorname {sgn}(a_{3}-a_{1})\dots \operatorname {sgn}(a_{n}-a_{1})\operatorname {sgn}(a_{3}-a_{2})\operatorname {sgn}(a_{4}-a_{2})\dots \operatorname {sgn}(a_{n}-a_{2})\dots \operatorname {sgn}(a_{n}-a_{n-1})\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b4870ce8a8f3d9334594335adb11ddd4023f2f9c" style="vertical-align: -4.005ex; width:117.38ex; height:9.176ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where the product is totally antisymmetric in all indices, and the <a href="/wiki/Sign_function" title="Sign function">sign function</a> (denoted by "<span class="texhtml">sgn</span>") extracts the sign of each difference discarding the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_value" title="Absolute value">absolute value</a>. The formula is valid for all index values, and for any <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> (when <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> = 0 or 1, this is the <a href="/wiki/Empty_product" title="Empty product">empty product</a>). However, computing the formula above naively is <span class="texhtml">O(<i>n</i><sup>2</sup>)</span> in <a href="/wiki/Time_complexity" title="Time complexity">time complexity</a>, whereas the sign can be computed via the <a href="/wiki/Permutation#Cycle_notation" title="Permutation">disjoint cycles</a> of a permutation in only <span class="texhtml">O(<i>n</i> log(<i>n</i>))</span> cost.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">Properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tensor" title="Tensor">tensor</a> whose components in an <a href="/wiki/Orthonormal_basis" title="Orthonormal basis">orthonormal basis</a> are given by the Levi-Civita symbol (a tensor of <a href="/wiki/Covariance_and_contravariance_of_vectors" title="Covariance and contravariance of vectors">covariant</a> rank <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>) is sometimes called a <b>permutation tensor</b>. It is actually a <a href="/wiki/Pseudotensor" title="Pseudotensor">pseudotensor</a> because under an <a href="/wiki/Orthogonal_matrix" title="Orthogonal matrix">orthogonal transformation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jacobian_matrix_and_determinant" title="Jacobian matrix and determinant">Jacobian determinant</a> −1 (i.e., a <a href="/wiki/Rotation" title="Rotation">rotation</a> composed with a <a href="/wiki/Reflection_(mathematics)" title="Reflection (mathematics)">reflection</a>), it acquires a minus sign. As the Levi-Civita symbol is a pseudotensor, the result of taking a <a href="/wiki/Cross_product" title="Cross product">cross product</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Pseudovector" title="Pseudovector">pseudovector</a>, not a vector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riley_et_al_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Riley_et_al-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under a general <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coordinate_change" title="Coordinate change">coordinate change</a>, the components of the permutation tensor are multiplied by the <a href="/wiki/Jacobian_matrix_and_determinant" title="Jacobian matrix and determinant">Jacobian</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Transformation_matrix" title="Transformation matrix">transformation matrix</a>. This implies that in coordinate frames different from the one in which the tensor was defined, its components can differ from those of the Levi-Civita symbol by an overall factor. If the frame is orthonormal, the factor will be ±1 depending on whether the orientation of the frame is the same or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riley_et_al_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Riley_et_al-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In index-free tensor notation, the Levi-Civita symbol is replaced by the concept of the <a href="/wiki/Hodge_dual" title="Hodge dual">Hodge dual</a>.</p>
<p>In a context where tensor index notation is used to manipulate tensor components, the Levi-Civita symbol may be written with its indices as either subscripts or superscripts with no change in meaning, as might be convenient. Thus, one could write</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon ^{ij\dots k}=\varepsilon _{ij\dots k}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\varepsilon ^{ij\dots k}=\varepsilon _{ij\dots k}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5fd32b6d73d09566d729beb50bfe3c9443662691" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:14.532ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>In these examples, superscripts should be considered equivalent with subscripts.</p>
<p>Summation symbols can be eliminated by using <a href="/wiki/Einstein_notation" title="Einstein notation">Einstein notation</a>, where an index repeated between two or more terms indicates summation over that index. For example,</p>

</mrow>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Two_dimensions_2">Two dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Two dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_dimensions_2">Three dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Three dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Product">Product</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Product">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<p>A special case of this result is (<b><a href="#math_4">4</a></b>):</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
</mrow>
</munderover>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{i=1}^{3}\varepsilon _{ijk}\varepsilon _{imn}=\delta _{jm}\delta _{kn}-\delta _{jn}\delta _{km}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{i=1}^{3}\varepsilon _{ijk}\varepsilon _{imn}=\delta _{jm}\delta _{kn}-\delta _{jn}\delta _{km}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5e19d7782236c042cf847d11be2e7d1142738671" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:30.592ex; height:7.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>sometimes called the "<a href="/wiki/Tensor_contraction" title="Tensor contraction">contracted</a> epsilon identity".</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Einstein_notation" title="Einstein notation">Einstein notation</a>, the duplication of the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span> index implies the sum on <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span>. The previous is then denoted <span class="texhtml"><i>ε<sub>ijk</sub>ε<sub>imn</sub></i> = <i>δ<sub>jm</sub>δ<sub>kn</sub></i> − <i>δ<sub>jn</sub>δ<sub>km</sub></i></span>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="n_dimensions"><i><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span></i> dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: n dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Index_and_symbol_values_2">Index and symbol values</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Index and symbol values">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<p>where the exclamation mark (<span class="texhtml">!</span>) denotes the <a href="/wiki/Factorial" title="Factorial">factorial</a>, and <span class="texhtml"><i>δ</i><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><i>α</i>…<br/>
<i>β</i>…</span></span> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generalized_Kronecker_delta" title="Generalized Kronecker delta">generalized Kronecker delta</a>. For any <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>, the property</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munderover>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>j</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>k</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mo>⋯<!-- ⋯ --></mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>

<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>

</mrow>

</msub>

<mi>n</mi>

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{i,j,k,\dots =1}^{n}\varepsilon _{ijk\dots }\varepsilon _{ijk\dots }=n!}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{i,j,k,\dots =1}^{n}\varepsilon _{ijk\dots }\varepsilon _{ijk\dots }=n!}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/04755c7661b3e7aa2931e71e2e57663103204add" style="vertical-align: -3.505ex; width:23.89ex; height:7.509ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>follows from the facts that</p>
<ul>
<li>every permutation is either even or odd,</li>
<li>(+1)<sup>2</sup> = (−1)<sup>2</sup> = 1, and</li>
<li>the number of permutations of any <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>-element set number is exactly <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i>!</span>.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Product_2">Product</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Product">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proofs">Proofs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Proofs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For (<b><a href="#math_1">1</a></b>), both sides are <a href="/wiki/Antisymmetric_tensor" title="Antisymmetric tensor">antisymmetric</a> with respect of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ij</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">mn</span>. We therefore only need to consider the case <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i> ≠ <i>j</i></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>m</i> ≠ <i>n</i></span>. By substitution, we see that the equation holds for <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i><sub>12</sub><i>ε</i><sup>12</sup></span>, i.e., for <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i> = <i>m</i> = 1</span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>j</i> = <i>n</i> = 2</span>. (Both sides are then one). Since the equation is antisymmetric in <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ij</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">mn</span>, any set of values for these can be reduced to the above case (which holds). The equation thus holds for all values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ij</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">mn</span>.</p>
<p>Using (<b><a href="#math_1">1</a></b>), we have for (<b><a href="#math_2">2</a></b>)</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{ij}\varepsilon ^{in}=\delta _{i}{}^{i}\delta _{j}{}^{n}-\delta _{i}{}^{n}\delta _{j}{}^{i}=2\delta _{j}{}^{n}-\delta _{j}{}^{n}=\delta _{j}{}^{n}\,.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\varepsilon _{ij}\varepsilon ^{in}=\delta _{i}{}^{i}\delta _{j}{}^{n}-\delta _{i}{}^{n}\delta _{j}{}^{i}=2\delta _{j}{}^{n}-\delta _{j}{}^{n}=\delta _{j}{}^{n}\,." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/30310b0d588a96f8a8efc22cf0bc78a864eca56a" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:43.969ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>Here we used the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Einstein_summation_convention" title="Einstein summation convention">Einstein summation convention</a> with <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span> going from 1 to 2. Next, (<b><a href="#math_3">3</a></b>) follows similarly from (<b><a href="#math_2">2</a></b>).</p>
<p>To establish (<b><a href="#math_5">5</a></b>), notice that both sides vanish when <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i> ≠ <i>j</i></span>. Indeed, if <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i> ≠ <i>j</i></span>, then one can not choose <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> such that both permutation symbols on the left are nonzero. Then, with <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i> = <i>j</i></span> fixed, there are only two ways to choose <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> from the remaining two indices. For any such indices, we have</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mi>m</mi>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>

<mi>i</mi>

</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{jmn}\varepsilon ^{imn}=\left(\varepsilon ^{imn}\right)^{2}=1}</annotation>
</semantics>

</dl>
<p>(no summation), and the result follows.</p>
<p>Then (<b><a href="#math_6">6</a></b>) follows since <span class="nowrap">3! = 6</span> and for any distinct indices <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i>, <i>j</i>, <i>k</i></span> taking values <span class="nowrap">1, 2, 3</span>, we have</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>

</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{ijk}\varepsilon ^{ijk}=1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\varepsilon _{ijk}\varepsilon ^{ijk}=1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/33ba3b3478ae1012e5485c43d07cf7767c6aa5a3" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:11.181ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span><span style="padding-left:3em;"> </span>(no summation, distinct <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i>, <i>j</i>, <i>k</i></span>)</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications_and_examples">Applications and examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Applications and examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Determinants">Determinants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Determinants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Linear_algebra" title="Linear algebra">linear algebra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Determinant" title="Determinant">determinant</a> of a <span class="nowrap">3 × 3</span> <a href="/wiki/Square_matrix" title="Square matrix">square matrix</a> <span class="texhtml"><b>A</b> = [<i>a<sub>ij</sub></i>]</span> can be written<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">det</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<munderover>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>j</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>
</munderover>

<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
<mi>j</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \det(\mathbf {A} )=\sum _{i=1}^{3}\sum _{j=1}^{3}\sum _{k=1}^{3}\varepsilon _{ijk}a_{1i}a_{2j}a_{3k}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\det(\mathbf {A} )=\sum _{i=1}^{3}\sum _{j=1}^{3}\sum _{k=1}^{3}\varepsilon _{ijk}a_{1i}a_{2j}a_{3k}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/beb98573a2c43f7234607ca48ac0605e2bef26a3" style="vertical-align: -3.338ex; width:33.966ex; height:7.676ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>Similarly the determinant of an <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> × <i>n</i></span> matrix <span class="texhtml"><b>A</b> = [<i>a<sub>ij</sub></i>]</span> can be written as<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riley_et_al_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Riley_et_al-5">[5]</a></sup></p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \det(\mathbf {A} )=\varepsilon _{i_{1}\dots i_{n}}a_{1i_{1}}\dots a_{ni_{n}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \det(\mathbf {A} )=\varepsilon _{i_{1}\dots i_{n}}a_{1i_{1}}\dots a_{ni_{n}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/624037b5e0d67e88f75559b3d8b8eef62708d378" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:28.339ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vector_cross_product">Vector cross product</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Vector cross product">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cross_product" title="Cross product">cross product</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cross_product_.28two_vectors.29">Cross product (two vectors)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cross product (two vectors)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>If <span class="texhtml"><b>a</b> = (<i>a</i><sup>1</sup>, <i>a</i><sup>2</sup>, <i>a</i><sup>3</sup>)</span> and <span class="texhtml"><b>b</b> = (<i>b</i><sup>1</sup>, <i>b</i><sup>2</sup>, <i>b</i><sup>3</sup>)</span> are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vector_(geometry)" title="Vector (geometry)">vectors</a> in <span class="texhtml">ℝ<sup>3</sup></span> (represented in some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-handed_coordinate_system" title="Right-handed coordinate system">right-handed coordinate system</a> using an <a href="/wiki/Orthonormal_basis" title="Orthonormal basis">orthonormal basis</a>), their <a href="/wiki/Cross_product" title="Cross product">cross product</a> can be written as a determinant:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riley_et_al_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-Riley_et_al-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>hence also using the Levi-Civita symbol, and more simply:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle (\mathbf {a\times b} )^{i}=\sum _{j=1}^{3}\sum _{k=1}^{3}\varepsilon _{ijk}a^{j}b^{k}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b798fa46e21c7f9d393a74a7c8abaf1de3d85f35" style="vertical-align: -3.338ex; width:27.276ex; height:7.676ex;"/></span></dd>

<p>In <a href="/wiki/Einstein_notation" title="Einstein notation">Einstein notation</a>, the summation symbols may be omitted, and the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span>th component of their cross product equals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kay_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kay-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">a</mi>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="bold">b</mi>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>j</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (\mathbf {a\times b} )^{i}=\varepsilon _{ijk}a^{j}b^{k}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle (\mathbf {a\times b} )^{i}=\varepsilon _{ijk}a^{j}b^{k}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d753218e19a64d5d50e10ee54c8b0e4d970fb842" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:19.771ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>The first component is</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Triple_scalar_product_.28three_vectors.29">Triple scalar product (three vectors)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Triple scalar product (three vectors)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>From the above expression for the cross product, we have:</p>

<p>If <span class="texhtml"><b>c</b> = (<i>c</i><sup>1</sup>, <i>c</i><sup>2</sup>, <i>c</i><sup>3</sup>)</span> is a third vector, then the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triple_scalar_product" title="Triple scalar product">triple scalar product</a> equals</p>

<p>From this expression, it can be seen that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triple_scalar_product" title="Triple scalar product">triple scalar product</a> is antisymmetric when exchanging any pair of arguments. For example,</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Curl_.28one_vector_field.29">Curl (one vector field)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Curl (one vector field)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>If <span class="texhtml"><b>F</b> = (<i>F</i><sup>1</sup>, <i>F</i><sup>2</sup>, <i>F</i><sup>3</sup>)</span> is a vector field defined on some <a href="/wiki/Open_set" title="Open set">open set</a> of <span class="texhtml">ℝ<sup>3</sup></span> as a <a href="/wiki/Function_(mathematics)" title="Function (mathematics)">function</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Position_vector" title="Position vector">position</a> <span class="texhtml"><b>x</b> = (<i>x</i><sup>1</sup>, <i>x</i><sup>2</sup>, <i>x</i><sup>3</sup>)</span> (using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinates" title="Cartesian coordinates">Cartesian coordinates</a>). Then the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">i</span>th component of the <a href="/wiki/Curl_(mathematics)" title="Curl (mathematics)">curl</a> of <span class="texhtml"><b>F</b></span> equals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kay_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kay-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∇<!-- ∇ --></mi>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>ε<!-- ε --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>j</mi>
<mi>k</mi>

<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>

</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (\nabla \times \mathbf {F} )^{i}(\mathbf {x} )=\varepsilon ^{ijk}{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{j}}}F_{k}(\mathbf {x} ),}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle (\nabla \times \mathbf {F} )^{i}(\mathbf {x} )=\varepsilon ^{ijk}{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{j}}}F_{k}(\mathbf {x} ),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2625839cc463a23c65629b86018e8a35a392ca8c" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:29.87ex; height:5.676ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>which follows from the cross product expression above, substituting components of the <a href="/wiki/Gradient" title="Gradient">gradient</a> vector <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_operator" title="Linear operator">operator</a> (nabla).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tensor_density">Tensor density</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tensor density">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In any arbitrary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curvilinear_coordinate_system" title="Curvilinear coordinate system">curvilinear coordinate system</a> and even in the absence of a <a href="/wiki/Metric_tensor" title="Metric tensor">metric</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Manifold" title="Manifold">manifold</a>, the Levi-Civita symbol as defined above may be considered to be a <a href="/wiki/Tensor_density" title="Tensor density">tensor density</a> field in two different ways. It may be regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Covariance_and_contravariance_of_vectors" title="Covariance and contravariance of vectors">contravariant</a> tensor density of weight +1 or as a <a href="/wiki/Covariance_and_contravariance_of_vectors" title="Covariance and contravariance of vectors">covariant</a> tensor density of weight −1. In <i>n</i> dimensions using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generalized_Kronecker_delta" title="Generalized Kronecker delta">generalized Kronecker delta</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<p>Notice that these are numerically identical. In particular, the sign is the same.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Levi-Civita_tensors">Levi-Civita tensors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Levi-Civita tensors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On a <a href="/wiki/Pseudo-Riemannian_manifold" title="Pseudo-Riemannian manifold">pseudo-Riemannian manifold</a>, one may define a coordinate-invariant covariant tensor field whose coordinate representation agrees with the Levi-Civita symbol wherever the coordinate system is such that the basis of the tangent space is orthonormal with respect to the metric and matches a selected orientation. This tensor should not be confused with the tensor density field mentioned above. The presentation in this section closely follows <a href="#CITEREFCarroll2004">Carroll 2004</a>.</p>
<p>The covariant Levi-Civita tensor (also known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riemannian_volume_form" title="Riemannian volume form">Riemannian volume form</a>) in a given coordinate system is</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mrow>
<mo>|</mo>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">det</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
<msub>
<mi>g</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>a</mi>
<mi>b</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>
<mo>|</mo>
</mrow>
</msqrt>
</mrow>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Example:_Minkowski_Space">Example: Minkowski Space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Example: Minkowski Space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 4D <a href="/wiki/Minkowski_space" title="Minkowski space">Minkowski space</a> (the four-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">spacetime</a> of <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>), the covariant Levi-Civita tensor is</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mi>α<!-- α --></mi>
<mi>β<!-- β --></mi>
<mi>γ<!-- γ --></mi>
<mi>δ<!-- δ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">det</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
<msub>
<mi>g</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle E_{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }={\sqrt {|\det[g_{\mu \nu }]|}}\,\varepsilon _{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }\,,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e90dc84fea8ffc3c3e8f903bb673ac09b338b460" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:26.98ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span></dd>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle E^{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }=g^{\alpha \zeta }g^{\beta \eta }g^{\gamma \theta }g^{\delta \iota }E_{\zeta \eta \theta \iota }\,.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b56d190e0afba6ce5313d59b47b0985e2cb3ba79" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:26.875ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E^{\mu _{1}\dots \mu _{p}\alpha _{1}\dots \alpha _{n-p}}E_{\mu _{1}\dots \mu _{p}\beta _{1}\dots \beta _{n-p}}=-p!\delta _{\beta _{1}\dots \beta _{n-p}}^{\alpha _{1}\dots \alpha _{n-p}}\,,}</annotation>

<p>where <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>α<!-- α --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
</msubsup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \delta _{\beta _{1}\dots \beta _{n-p}}^{\alpha _{1}\dots \alpha _{n-p}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \delta _{\beta _{1}\dots \beta _{n-p}}^{\alpha _{1}\dots \alpha _{n-p}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2d85718caa6b461d362461001dde3c9fded4904b" style="vertical-align: -1.671ex; width:8.878ex; height:4.009ex;"/></span> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generalized_Kronecker_delta" title="Generalized Kronecker delta">generalized Kronecker delta</a>. The following are some examples of this identity:</p>
<dl>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}E_{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }E_{\rho \sigma \mu \nu }&amp;\equiv g_{\alpha \zeta }g_{\beta \eta }g_{\gamma \theta }g_{\delta \iota }\delta _{\rho \sigma \mu \nu }^{\zeta \eta \theta \iota }\\E^{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }E^{\rho \sigma \mu \nu }&amp;\equiv g^{\alpha \zeta }g^{\beta \eta }g^{\gamma \theta }g^{\delta \iota }\delta _{\zeta \eta \theta \iota }^{\rho \sigma \mu \nu }\\E^{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }E_{\rho \beta \gamma \delta }&amp;\equiv -6\delta _{\rho }^{\alpha }\\E^{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }E_{\rho \sigma \gamma \delta }&amp;\equiv -2\delta _{\rho \sigma }^{\alpha \beta }\\E^{\alpha \beta \gamma \delta }E_{\rho \sigma \theta \delta }&amp;\equiv -\delta _{\rho \sigma \theta }^{\alpha \beta \gamma }\,.\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Levi-Civita_symbol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: External links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
